< review>
It is really rare for me to give a bad review, but my experience at AAA in Alameda near In N Out was not only costly, but also was in poor taste.

I visited to request title duplicates for vehicles I meant to eventually sell. I opened the door to be greeted by someone at the front whose face looked very puzzled kind of like "what are you doing here" asking, "do you need something?". Maybe she was just intrigued about an unfamiliar customer, but no smiles.

I mean that's not too big a deal, but it really set the tone for what was to come.

I let her know I would like to request duplicate titles for 4 vehicles and she gave me 4 dmv pink forms. I didn't receive any guidance on filling them out, but that's okay.

I filled out the forms for 4 vehicles to request dupes for which took a while. I then entered and was asked to sit and wait.

My turn came to see a representative to turn in the forms and I stepped up to speak with her. She looked at the forms and she scanned them with her eyes. She then looked at me and asked, "are you just trying to sell these vehicles?". I said "yes, and I would like to have the titles handy so that I can have smooth time selling them." She said, "it takes up to 30 days to receive a title in the mail. It is faster to just bring the the customer to sign the forms". I then insisted, "i want to offer confidence the next buyer because the last customer bailed because we didn't have the title handy. I want to avoid that from happening again". Exasperatedly the rep said, "if you want to sell it sooner, you're better off just bringing the customer into the dmv or aaa and transferring the title on the same form." It's true. There is a way for titles to transfer this way, but the caveat is for only those wish to register the vehicle in California. My dad who was with me was also convinced by this notion and voted that we skip out on trying to get the duplicates. I had already filled out four of these forms and waited, but I conceded based on the expert advice. I didn't anticipate this caveat that I mentioned, registration limited to CA without the title, and low and behold, 1 month later, my next interested party is from Mexico. I replicate the process advised by the AAA rep expert who informed me and was knocked by the fact that the customers didn't need to register the vehicles in CA.

The fact that I insisted in my interest for titles, but was talked out of it and not really met with any useful help, just makes me kick myself for trusting them there. I think the reason behind why she suggested me to come back with the customer  was because they were open for limited hours and I might have filled it out improperly and just didn't want to bother with me.

This review might come as a surprise to some or just be met with criticism for my naivete or sore loss, but is it too much to expect from a paid membership to be met with expertise and care for the customer?

I don't know what it is, but I feel belittled by this office and somewhat cheated. Luckily the customer is flexible and is ready to buy still, but this experience with AAA was an unexpected cost of money and time.

Hate all you want on this, but this is what you get from me. I only wish there was a Yelp page to add another bad review. I feel like they misinformed me and disuaded me from improving my legal standing on my property. Why did i listen? My suggestion is don't listen to these reps and they don't know anything. From the greeter to the assistant. That's it.< /review>

I deleted my 5 star rating to give a 1 star because of being refused service.
The past 2 years, every single morning, I come here to indulge in my venti blonde roast coffee appetite, order a breakfast sandwich if I like, and take advantage of the free wi-fi.
Now, with no warning or heads up, I am refused a fifty cents refill because of the barista who served me was no longer at the cash register. This is not the way you do business or treat customers, a regular customer, at that. My feelings are hurt.
This is an establishment I have become loyal to. I do not go to any other coffee shop, until now. I am taking my $350 Starbucks monthly budget somewhere else where I will not be offended.
This experience is not going to stop at this Google review.  I am taking this further to corporate office, yelp, yahoo, etc...

I, now, understand why Starbucks is closing 500 stores nationwide because of business lose.</review>

< text>
Dec 1999.  I had not been to a dentist in several years.  I found Sunnyvale Dental Care in my insurance booklet, and it looked like they could do most every procedure I thought I would need without my having to call other offices.  I was already embarrassed about my teeth, and I didn't want to have to call all over explaining how I let them get so bad.  So I nervously called Sunnyvale Dental Care, made that first appointment, ... and I have been going back ever since, including two weeks ago when I needed a routine cleaning and exam. That's almost 17 years as a patient.

Dr. Antonious is extremely talented and conscientious.  He is qualified/trained for most any procedure you might need, and if he thinks you should consider a specialist for certain procedures, he'll let you know.  I know, because he's done this for me.

Dr. Antonious has tried for years to help me hold on to the teeth I have remaining.  He has never recommended procedures I have not needed, and he is very aware of my desire to minimize costs while maximizing care. Dr. Antonious has seen me in off hours for emergency situations, too.  He always makes me feel comfortable with the work he is doing, and he always takes pride in doing great work.  Sound like I'm happy with my dentist?  I AM.  And with all of his staff, too.

I hope you will not need any of the work I have needed, but if you do, you can feel good about trying Dr. Antonious/Sunnyvale Dental Care.  I attest to his abilities, and I recommend him to friends who ask.<//text>

The place wasn't really all that bad. I was in town on vacation from Arizona. I was there Tuesday night celebrating my  50th Birthday along with my Sister and 2 very close  friends from high school. These 3 have visited this establishment several times for they are from the area. At first, upon walking in, they  made us feel welcomed and were attentive to our needs and answered my concerns for I have food allergies. Our server, don't recall ever getting her name, at first seemed like she was happy to have us. We 4 can be a very lively group. Well the moment a large party walked in, she was more attentive to them even though their group wasn't all there. She never came back to check on us. Best sushi I ever had, bar none. For the Antelope Valley, it's crazy that we find a restaurant this good when about everything else is garbage. Even on an international point if view, it's litterally amazing!

The fish is fresh, delicious, tender, buttery and their interpretations of the classics are phenomenal. You NEED to try the "Maine Roll" (a baked lobster sushi concoction that's just demented).

They have a "all you can eat" sushi bar and happy hour sak√©, so bring your appetite and enjoy sushi after sushi until your belly pops.

I much prefer the ambiance of this small restaurant (compared to the Palmdale location) as it feels more Japan-typical and cozy.

Definitely a 10/10 for me!</Review>
